<Rating>5</Rating><review>Food here is LEGIT! Pho, just like ramen, is the perfect food after a day in the snow. On our way back from Dodge Ridge, we stopped here and were pleasantly surprised. The soup for the combination pho was so good (this is coming from a person who's very picky about pho), it was slightly sweet but didn't have any MSG flavor. It was also a great value, with lots of meat and tripes. My favorite was actually the spring roll. The freshly grilled pork had a great flavorful, perfect with Sriracha peanut sauce. I literally could not stop eating and even took half from my boyfriend :p the spicy chicken fried noodle was good too, nice wok flavor and pretty spicy. I'm not a big fan of pepper seeds in my food so if they had use fresh chili or powder, it would have been even better.

Thai iced tea is made fresh in the house, so you have to give it a try.

We came on a Sunday afternoon during off hours, and this place still had a few tables of customers, surprisingly. <date>1490922362443< /date>< Text>
Food is good!

Service by one of the servers was FABULOUS. Lady server (she had braces).

The guy server was horrible! The type of server that just shouldn't be serving. Asked for veggies, then when he came with that, I realized they forgot to give us water, so I asked whenever he had a chance, to bring the water. He replied, "you should have told me that before, when I was getting your vegetables."

Ummmmm. Ok. I asked when I ordered. But, I guess the gal who took our order didn't relay the message to him, so our water was not delivered until half way into the meal. And, I heard the guy server tell the lady server to get it, and so she did, in between dropping food off to other tables.

Not impressed by the male server.

So, if you go here with the intention that you might get subpar service, but yummy food, you'll like it here.

Pho soup base was great, but the cuts of meat was mostly cartilage.

I had a chicken, vegetable, noodle bowl. It's like a cold noodle salad. The flavor was great. Good portion for the price.

We still paid about $30 with tip which isn't horrible, we had 1 pho, 1 chicken/noodle bowl, gyoza appetizer, 1 Vietnamese iced coffee, and boba Thai iced tea.

Again the food was good, service is good if you get the nice server. üòÜ</Text>

<Text>Okay, so they told me not to say this, but I really enjoyed the way they had their hands in my mouth.

Jokes aside, I think Pearl Dental is the reason I started going to the dentist regularly again. I hadn't gone for years, but when I needed to get my wisdom teeth out, Pearl was the closest place to my work with positive reviews, so I gave them a try. I was satisfied with how painless the process of scheduling and billing was. They even send me text reminders because I like to forget that I have appointments coming up. The wisdom tooth removal was pretty easy as well. I wanted to "steal" one of my molars to keep because it looked cool, so they offered to clean it before I put it in my pocket lol. Since my first visit there, there have been times when I didn't have dental insurance, but they were willing to work with me with the out-of-pocket costs. Oh, and the staff is super friendly! I like that they have conversations with you even though you can't speak while your mouth is open. Don't like to talk? They can be quiet too. I'm going to keep going to Pearl Dental as long as I live in the area. Oh, and Gloria kindly reminded me to leave this review. I kept telling them that I was going to leave one, but I"m so bad about these things.

< text>
After getting into an accident late last month I was in need of a new car when my old one was declared a total loss. I didn't have much of a budget so I had started at a spot in gardena that held auctions. I almost pulled the trigger on a car, but after talking to my friends I held back.

I did some research and found some cars at local dealerships, but each had some recent terrible reviews. When I came across AutoBoyz I couldn't believe the 5-star reviews across the board on both Yelp and Google Reviews.  I live in Culver City, but made it a point to at least go and check out their inventory.

Upon arriving I was greeted by Bob who politely told me if I had any questions to let him know. I was then left alone to check out their current inventory. I came across a 2014 Volkswagen Jetta, which I really liked. I asked for the CarFax and what it would cost out the door. Bob gave me a print out copy of the CarFax as well as a full breakdown of what it would cost. I ended up leaving to check out some more cars at other dealerships to compare, but left happy with the no hassle experience.

After running in to the typical pushy car salesman I came back to AutoBoyz the next day. Bob walked me through all the paperwork thoroughly and I drove off in a new pre-owned vehicle for myself. A+ Customer Service, I highly suggest stopping by AutoBoyz if you're in the market for pre-owned vehicle.< /text>

<rating>4</rating><Resp>None</Resp><Text>Complicated review here. 4 stars not because I loved the place nor because it wasn't a nice place to eat or the fact that their food was/is great or not.

The bathroom was the only negative item that stood out immensely; not a restroom anyone would prefer to use unless absolutely needed to. It was busy so maybe they didn't get a chance to freshen it up for a while.

I never been to a "Hawaiian" joint before and had no expectations, but it was referred by a local-ish person who said many great things about the food. I had no idea what to order or what I actually ordered. Not a huge fan of sushi but found out the "55" was sorta a sushi bowl with pork. It wasn't not great, but I have no acquired taste of it as of yet. The Cola drink was not a Cola drink, more like a flavored soda water. In terms of atmosphere and service I have to say, it was peaceful, comfortable and had a hometown feel to it. Most at my table were not satisfied with their orders but my sister who is a vegetarian loved the food she ordered (apologies for not memorizing her order).

When in town I would like to try this place again and do a bit more research on the food itself prior to ordering.< /Text><pics>None</pics>< username>

<text>I was on the fence about whether to give Pono's 3 or 4 stars. I think 3.5 stars is probably more accurate. They share the space they are in with a separate business (the Reef Bar), which means if you order food from the counter at Pono's (and want anything other than some canned Hawaiian Sun sinks), you then have to order and pay for drinks separately from the Reef Bar. Kind of a hassle. Also, here's yet another eatery where it's mostly self service (order at the counter and they bring your order to your table when ready) but their Point of Sale terminal defaults to asking you to leaving a 15-25% tip...Hmm. On the plus side, it's a nice casual space with plenty of indoor and outdoor (pet-friendly) seating. Pono has a pretty vast menu of apps, salads, bowls, plate lunches, burgers, and more. We tried the Coconut Shrimp Appetizer, which was ok, but shrimp was a bit small and overdone. (Not as good as Coconuts Maui Fish House in Cupertino or Hawaii). My spouse ordered the Chicken Teriyaki Plate which was decent (2 pieces of boneless dark meat) and comes with rice, and choice of Mac salad or coleslaw. I ordered the Braddah Poke Salad which comes loaded with Ahi Poke, over mixed greens, cucumber, edamame, canned mandarin oranges, seaweed salad, kimchi, and pickled ginger. Good portion, ahi poke was pretty fresh, not crazy about the canned mandarin oranges. Overall, food was decent but not particularly memorable.<//text>< pics>

<Review>Great food, good drinks, great music! What else could you ask for ?
Pono is in a decent place in town and is easily accessible. I wish there was a bit more parking, but anywhere downtown is rough to park at. Everything on the menu here is delicious and the live music makes the experience much more pleasant as well. They also have nice outdoor seating. My reason for 4 stars instead of 5 is because the last time I was here, and this haooens often, the bartender was very slow, we had to ask our waittress if the food was coming because we saw it in the window ready to go for at least 5 minutes without anyone taking it, and the waitress didn't engage with us in any way when they brought our food out even though there were a few things we needed. The waitress was very nice, but just not paying attention much. This was during a dead time when we were one of the only customers there.

< review>
Hard to find using GPS but totally worth it. My husband gives a odd ball review considering it was our first time and only ordered two dishes. Beware of generalized reviews is all I have to say. I grew up in around Hawaiians and anything goes with rice including macaroni salad, which was delicious. Live music, Full bar, tropical outside and inside patio seating made this place fun. We ordered the Kahuku style sauteed prawns and Hawian Kalua pork. The servings were generous. Kudos to the chef's in the kitchen!</review>

<name>Jim Brown< /name>< Date>
1497416111166< /Date>
< Rating>
3< /Rating>
< text>
It's always amateur hour at this cross between a local music spot and Hawaiian-theme menu. Service is sometimes friendly, always unskilled, sometimes the kitchen puts something fairly close to the menu description on your plate. On the plus side, the food is often fairly tasty and fresh, outside seating is quite pleasant, and dogs are welcome. That's good, because inside can get very noisy when there's music.

There's a bar, but no waitress service, so after ordering and paying for food at the front door counter, you stand in line again at the bar. The closest thing to service is that someone brings your food to your table. It's hard to get a menu of the little dishes, which is mostly what I want to order, so it's always a hassle figuring that out.

I really wanted to give this place 4 stars for the times they get it right, but that's only about half the time, so it's 3.< /text>

< text>
The only good thing this place has going on is that is open til 11pm on certain days. Otherwise, the service is terrible, food is average. I tried the Pono's BBQ combo, which had Chicken Teriyaki, Beef Teriyaki, & Kal-Bi Ribs. The combo comes with rice and mac and cheese. Chicken and beef were fine, but the ribs were what I would say, a bit carbonized to my liking.  At the time there was a live band playing hawaain music and it was very loud; when we looked for a place to sit, only couple of tables available were dirty. I asked a waiter to clean one, and she never came back, so I went to the register and asked for a rag so I could clean the table myself. On my 2nd visit I tried the pork Lau Lau as I had never had it and it was tasteless, not to say a bit bitter. I forced myself to eat it, but definitly not a good experience. Not sure what pork lau lau is supposed to taste like, but I wouldn't order that again, at least at this joint. The desserts on the other hand, were good. But overall, the staff needs to do their job there and at least clean the tables.<//text>

< Review>
Went for the first time after living nearby for a couple years. The first thing that struck me was that the poke menu was hard to navigate, no prices anywhere but I guess it's catch price probably so you have to ask at the register. The pictures online look incredible, I had to try it.
I got a Salmon Ceviche bowl. I don't know if I ordered it wrong, but it looked nothing like the dozens of pictures posted. At first sight it was a bowl of Rice, Seaweed salad, and tons of Ginger. After digging the ginger off the top I did find about a half cup of salmon and tomato. It might've just been a bad night to go, it was totally empty at 6pm. I also got hotwings, and at $8 for 8 wings I'd suggest going elsewhere in town.
Props to the bartender though. She was super sweet and the happy hour Margarita was on point for $5, I might return just for that. And over all the service was good, just disappointed by the food and the portion size.<//Review>

<Date>1491961967356<//Date><rate>2</rate><Text>Ok ill be nice,
Being from maui its hard to find legit hawaiian food on the mainland because there is none, and I dont give a damn what L &L claims cause that food/crap is not hawaiian! Anyways I had the Ali'i plate because when I saw the lau lau, I just had to get one! Lau lau in da mainland!? I thought i found my missing part in life, but i was sadly halted in a small awakening and somewhat hit by reality...."duh we in the mainland!" It was dry, my braddah,  mr chef, please dont be shy with da hawaiian salt please just give em!" Also one or two more luau leaf would've  helped. Cut it smaller, lau lau supposed to be juicy and meaty, one part shoulder and or butt and another part belly for fat. But the kalua pig was good. Lomi salmon..... nice rendition but not the same. Im pretty sure the salted diced Salmon is cheaper than fresh salmon, so make it like how we eat it at home! Or not, its your buisiness. <gmapID>0x808e402f4083b061:0xc45909b9a2dda43b< /gmapID><user_name>Jason T<//user_name>< review>
There are tens of poke places opening up everywhere in California. This place takes it to a different level. We came on a saturday night. They had a live band that did some covers. We're not locals, but really enjoyed the atmosphere.

We had the Pono Poke plate. 2 scoops of rice, edamame, seaweed salad, and ahi. They have different flavor ones, we got the garlic ginger one if i remember correctly. We also got the kaluha pork fries to share. It was really delicious.

The people here are also very friendly and there were people of all ages out that night. So, it's very open. I love the beach town atmosphere even when it was freezing outside in the middle of november.

There 's a Reef Bar attached and they serve great micro brews on tap as well as some special drinks.</review>
